class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;tr&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="137"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>x<span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="139"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>10010</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="140"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tr&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tbody&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/table&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="141"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>In <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Computer_science" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Computer_science</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Computer science</span>"&gt;</span>computer science<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> and <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_theory" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Information_theory</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Information theory</span>"&gt;</span>information theory<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, a <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>Huffman code<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span> is a particular type of optimal <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prefix_code" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Prefix_code</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Prefix code</span>"&gt;</span>prefix code<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> that is commonly used for <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Lossless_data_compression" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Lossless_data_compression</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Lossless data compression</span>"&gt;</span>lossless data compression<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>. The process of finding or using such a code proceeds by means of <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>Huffman coding<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span>, an algorithm developed by <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_A._Huffman" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/David_A._Huffman</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">David A. Huffman</span>"&gt;</span>David A. Huffman<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> while he was a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Doctor_of_Science" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Doctor_of_Science</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Doctor of Science</span>"&gt;</span>Sc.D.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> student at <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Massachusetts_Institute_of_Technology</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Massachusetts Institute of Technology</span>"&gt;</span>MIT<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, and published in the 1952 paper "A Method for the Construction of Minimum-Redundancy Codes".<span class="html-tag">&lt;sup <span class="html-attribute-name">id</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">cite_ref-1</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">reference</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huffman_coding#cite_note-1" rel="noreferrer noopener">#cite_note-1</a>"&gt;</span>&amp;#91;1&amp;#93;<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/sup&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="142"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>The output from Huffman's algorithm can be viewed as a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable-length_code" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Variable-length_code</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Variable-length code</span>"&gt;</span>variable-length code<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> table for encoding a source symbol (such as a character in a file).  The algorithm derives this table from the estimated probability or frequency of occurrence (<span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>weight<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>) for each possible value of the source symbol.  As in other <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Entropy_encoding" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Entropy_encoding</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Entropy encoding</span>"&gt;</span>entropy encoding<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> methods, more common symbols are generally represented using fewer bits than less common symbols.  Huffman's method can be efficiently implemented, finding a code in time <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear_time" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Linear_time</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Linear time</span>"&gt;</span>linear<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> to the number of input weights if these weights are sorted.<span class="html-tag">&lt;sup <span class="html-attribute-name">id</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">cite_ref-2</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">reference</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huffman_coding#cite_note-2" rel="noreferrer noopener">#cite_note-2</a>"&gt;</span>&amp;#91;2&amp;#93;<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/sup&gt;</span>  However, although optimal among methods encoding symbols History</span>"&gt;</span>edit<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-tag">&lt;/h2&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="185"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>In 1951, <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/David_A._Huffman" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/David_A._Huffman</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">David A. Huffman</span>"&gt;</span>David A. Huffman<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> and his <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/MIT" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/MIT</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">MIT</span>"&gt;</span>MIT<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_theory" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Information_theory</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Information theory</span>"&gt;</span>information theory<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> classmates were given the choice of a term paper or a final <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Exam" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Exam</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Exam</span>"&gt;</span>exam<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>. The professor, <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Robert_M._Fano" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Robert_M._Fano</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Robert M. Fano</span>"&gt;</span>Robert M. Fano<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, assigned a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Term_paper" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Term_paper</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Term paper</span>"&gt;</span>term paper<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> on the problem of finding the most efficient binary code. Huffman, unable to prove any codes were the most efficient, was about to give up and start studying for the final when he hit upon the idea of using a frequency-sorted <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_tree" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Binary_tree</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Binary tree</span>"&gt;</span>binary tree<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> and quickly proved this method the most efficient.<span class="html-tag">&lt;sup <span class="html-attribute-name">id</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">cite_ref-5</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">reference</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Huffman_coding#cite_note-5" rel="noreferrer noopener">#cite_note-5</a>"&gt;</span>&amp;#91;5&amp;#93;<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/sup&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="186"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>In doing so, Huffman outdid Fano, who had worked with <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_theory" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Information_theory</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Information theory</span>"&gt;</span>information theory<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> inventor <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Claude_Shannon" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Claude_Shannon</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Claude Shannon</span>"&gt;</span>Claude Shannon<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> to develop a similar code.  Building the tree from the bottom up guaranteed optimality, unlike the top-down approach of <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shannon%E2%80%93Fano_coding" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Shannon%E2%80%93Fano_coding</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">ShannonFano coding</span>"&gt;</span>ShannonFano coding<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="187"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="188"></td><td class="line-content"><span Terminology</span>"&gt;</span>edit<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-tag">&lt;/h2&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="189"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>Huffman coding uses a specific method for choosing the representation for each symbol, resulting in a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Prefix_code" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Prefix_code</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Prefix code</span>"&gt;</span>prefix code<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> (sometimes called "prefix-free codes", that is, the bit string representing some particular symbol is never a prefix of the bit string representing any other symbol).  Huffman coding is such a widespread method for creating prefix codes that the term "Huffman code" is widely used as a synonym for "prefix code" even when such a code is not produced by Huffman's algorithm.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="190"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="191"></td><td class="html-tag">&lt;/tr&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tbody&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/table&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="662"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>For any code that is <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>biunique<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>, meaning that the code is <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Variable-length_code#Uniquely_decodable_codes" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Variable-length_code#Uniquely_decodable_codes</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Variable-length code</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>uniquely decodeable<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, the sum of the probability budgets across all symbols is always less than or equal to one. In this example, the sum is strictly equal to one; as a result, the code is termed a <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>complete<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span> code. If this is not the case, one can always derive an equivalent code by adding extra symbols (with associated null probabilities), to make the code complete while keeping it <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>biunique<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="663"></td><td class="line-content"><span formula above.)</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="855"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>As a consequence of <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Shannon%27s_source_coding_theorem" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Shannon%27s_source_coding_theorem</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Shannon&amp;#39;s source coding theorem</span>"&gt;</span>Shannon's source coding theorem<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, the entropy is a measure of the smallest codeword length that is theoretically possible for the given alphabet with associated weights. In this example, the weighted average codeword length is 2.25 bits per symbol, only slightly larger than the calculated entropy of 2.205 bits per symbol. So not only is this code optimal in the sense that no other feasible code performs better, but it is very close to the theoretical limit established by Shannon.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="856"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>In general, a Huffman code need not be unique. class="html-tag">&lt;mn&gt;</span>0.2<span class="html-tag">&lt;/mn&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="920"></td><td class="line-content">        <span class="html-tag">&lt;mo&gt;</span>;<span class="html-tag">&lt;/mo&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="921"></td><td class="line-content">        <span class="html-tag">&lt;mn&gt;</span>0.05<span class="html-tag">&lt;/mn&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="922"></td><td class="line-content">        <span class="html-tag">&lt;mo <span class="html-attribute-name">fence</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">false</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">stretchy</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">false</span>"&gt;</span>}<span class="html-tag">&lt;/mo&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="923"></td><td class="line-content">      <span class="html-tag">&lt;/mstyle&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="924"></td><td class="line-content">    <span class="html-tag">&lt;/mrow&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="925"></td><td class="line-content">    <span class="html-tag">&lt;annotation <span class="html-attribute-name">encoding</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">application/x-tex</span>"&gt;</span>{\displaystyle \{0.4;0.35;0.2;0.05\}}<span class="html-tag">&lt;/annotation&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="926"></td><td class="line-content">  <span class="html-tag">&lt;/semantics&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="927"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/math&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;img <span class="html-attribute-name">src</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-resource-link" target="_blank" href="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/09d9a62726a39dba09cc351e882ce53aac27f8c9" rel="noreferrer noopener">https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/09d9a62726a39dba09cc351e882ce53aac27f8c9</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-fallback-image-inline</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">aria-hidden</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">true</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">style</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:19.639ex; height:2.843ex;</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">alt</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">\{0.4;0.35;0.2;0.05\}</span>"/&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span>. A binary tree is generated from left to right taking the two least probable symbols and putting them together to form another equivalent symbol having a probability that equals the sum of the two symbols. The process is repeated until there is just one symbol. The tree can then be read backwards, from right to left, assigning different bits to different branches. The final Huffman code is: <span class="html-tag">&lt;table <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">wikitable</span>"&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;tbody&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;th&gt;</span>Symbol<span class="html-tag">&lt;/th&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;th&gt;</span>Code <span class="html-tag">&lt;/th&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>a1<span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>0 <span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>a2<span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>10 <span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>a3<span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>110 <span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>a4<span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;td&gt;</span>111 <span class="html-tag">&lt;/td&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/tr&gt;</span> <span class="html-tag">&lt;/tbody&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/table&gt;</span> The standard way to represent a signal made of 4 symbols is by using 2 bits/symbol, but the <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Information_entropy" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Information_entropy</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Information entropy</span>"&gt;</span>entropy<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> of the source is 1.74 bits/symbol. If this Huffman code is used to represent the signal, then the average length is lowered to 1.85 bits/symbol; it is still far from the theoretical limit because the probabilities of the symbols are different from negative powers of two.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/div&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/div&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/div&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="928"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>The technique works by creating a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Binary_tree" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Binary_tree</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Binary tree</span>"&gt;</span>binary tree<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> of nodes. These can be stored in a regular <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Array_data_type" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Array_data_type</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Array data type</span>"&gt;</span>array<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, the size of which depends on the number of symbols, <span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-element</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">style</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">display: none;</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;math <span class="html-attribute-name">xmlns</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML</span>"  <span class="html-attribute-name">alttext</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">{\displaystyle n}</span>"&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="929"></td><td class="line-content">  <span class="html-tag">&lt;semantics&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="930"></td><td class="line-content">    <span class="html-tag">&lt;mrow <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">MJX-TeXAtom-ORD</span>"&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="931"></td><td class="line-content">      <span class="html-tag">&lt;mstyle <span class="html-attribute-name">displaystyle</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">true</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">scriptlevel</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">0</span>"&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="932"></td><td class="line-content">        <span class="html-tag">&lt;mi&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/annotation&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="936"></td><td class="line-content">  <span class="html-tag">&lt;/semantics&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="937"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/math&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;img <span class="html-attribute-name">src</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-resource-link" target="_blank" href="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a601995d55609f2d9f5e233e36fbe9ea26011b3b" rel="noreferrer class="html-attribute-value">n</span>"/&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span>. A node can be either a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Leaf_node" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Leaf_node</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Leaf node</span>"&gt;</span>leaf node<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> or an <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Internal_node" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Internal_node</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Internal node</span>"&gt;</span>internal node<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>. Initially, all nodes are leaf nodes, which contain the <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>symbol<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span> itself, the <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>weight<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span> (frequency of appearance) of the symbol and optionally, a link to a <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>parent<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span> node which makes it easy to read the code (in reverse) starting from a leaf node. Internal nodes contain a <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>weight<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span>, links to <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>two child nodes<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span> and an optional link to a <span class="html-tag">&lt;b&gt;</span>parent<span class="html-tag">&lt;/b&gt;</span> node. As a common convention, bit '0' represents following the left child and bit '1' represents following the right child. A finished tree has up to <span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-element</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y</span>" <span n}</span>"&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="938"></td><td class="line-content">  <span class="html-tag">&lt;semantics&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" class="html-tag">&lt;/mi&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="942"></td><td class="line-content">      <span class="html-tag">&lt;/mstyle&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="html-tag">&lt;/mi&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="951"></td><td class="line-content">        <span class="html-tag">&lt;mo&gt;</span>&amp;#x2212;<span class="html-comment">&lt;!--  --&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/mo&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="952"></td><td class="line-content">        <span class="line-number" value="955"></td><td class="line-content">    <span class="html-tag">&lt;annotation <span class="html-attribute-name">encoding</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">application/x-tex</span>"&gt;</span>{\displaystyle n-1}<span class="html-tag">&lt;/annotation&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="956"></td><td class="line-content">  <span class="html-tag">&lt;/semantics&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="957"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/math&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;img <span class="html-attribute-name">src</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-resource-link" target="_blank" href="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fbd0b0f32b28f51962943ee9ede4fb34198a2521" rel="noreferrer noopener">https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/fbd0b0f32b28f51962943ee9ede4fb34198a2521</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-fallback-image-inline</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">aria-hidden</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">true</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">style</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">vertical-align: -0.505ex; width:5.398ex; height:2.343ex;</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">alt</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">n-1</span>"/&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span> internal nodes. A Huffman tree that omits unused symbols produces the most optimal code lengths.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="958"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>The process begins with the leaf nodes containing the probabilities of the symbol they represent. Then, the process takes the two nodes with smallest probability, and creates a new internal node having these two nodes as children. The weight of the new node is set to the sum of the weight of the children. We then apply the process again, on the new internal node and on the remaining nodes (i.e., we exclude the two leaf nodes), we repeat this process until only one node remains, which is the root of the Huffman tree.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="959"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>The simplest construction algorithm uses a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Priority_queue" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Priority_queue</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Priority queue</span>"&gt;</span>priority queue<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> where the node with lowest probability is given highest priority:</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="960"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="961"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;ol&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Create a leaf node for each symbol and add it to the priority queue.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="962"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>While there is more than one node in the queue:</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="963"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;ol&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Remove the two nodes of highest priority (lowest probability) from the queue<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="964"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Create a new internal node with these two nodes as children and with probability equal to the sum of the two nodes' probabilities.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="965"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Add the new node to the queue.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/ol&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="966"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>The remaining node is the root node and the tree is complete.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/ol&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="967"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>Since efficient priority queue data structures require O(log <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>) time per insertion, and a tree with <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span> leaves has 2<span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>1 nodes, this algorithm operates in O(<span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span> log <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>) time, where <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span> is the number of symbols.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="968"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>If the symbols are sorted by probability, there is a <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Linear-time" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Linear-time</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Linear-time</span>"&gt;</span>linear-time<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span> (O(<span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>)) method to create a Huffman tree using two <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Queue_(data_structure)" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Queue_(data_structure)</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-redirect</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Queue (data structure)</span>"&gt;</span>queues<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, the first one containing the initial weights (along with pointers to the associated leaves), and combined weights (along with pointers to the trees) being put in the back of the second queue. This assures that the lowest weight is always kept at the front of one of the two queues:</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="969"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="970"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;ol&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Start with as many leaves as there are symbols.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="971"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Enqueue all leaf nodes into the first queue (by probability in increasing order so that the least likely item is in the head of the queue).<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="972"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>While there is more than one node in the queues:</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="973"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;ol&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Dequeue the two nodes with the lowest weight by examining the fronts of both queues.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="974"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Create a new internal node, with the two just-removed nodes as children (either node can be either child) and the sum of their weights as the new weight.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="975"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Enqueue the new node into the rear of the second queue.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/ol&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="976"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>The remaining node is the root node; the tree has now been generated.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/ol&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="977"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>Once the Huffman tree has been generated, it is traversed to generate a dictionary which maps the symbols to binary codes as follows:</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="978"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="979"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;ol&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>Start with current node set to the root.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="980"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;li&gt;</span>If node is not a leaf node, label the edge to the left child as <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>0<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span> and the edge to the right child as <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>1<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span>. Repeat the process at both the left child and the right child.<span class="html-tag">&lt;/li&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/ol&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="981"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>The final encoding of any symbol is then read by a concatenation of the labels on the edges along the path from the root node to the symbol.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="982"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>In many cases, time complexity is not very important in the choice of algorithm here, since <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span> here is the number of symbols in the alphabet, which is typically a very small number (compared to the length of the message to be encoded); whereas complexity analysis concerns the behavior when <span class="html-tag">&lt;i&gt;</span>n<span class="html-tag">&lt;/i&gt;</span> grows to be very large.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="983"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>It is generally beneficial to minimize the variance of codeword length. For example, a communication buffer receiving Huffman-encoded data may need to be larger to deal with especially long symbols if the tree is especially unbalanced. To minimize variance, simply break ties between queues by choosing the item in the first queue.   This modification will retain the mathematical optimality of the Huffman coding while both minimizing variance and minimizing the length of the longest character code.</td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="984"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;/p&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="985"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;h3&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-headline</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">id</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Decompression</span>"&gt;</span>Decompression<span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-editsection</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-editsection-bracket</span>"&gt;</span>[<span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Huffman_coding&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" rel="noreferrer noopener">/w/index.php?title=Huffman_coding&amp;amp;action=edit&amp;amp;section=9</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Edit section: Decompression</span>"&gt;</span>edit<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mw-editsection-bracket</span>"&gt;</span>]<span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/span&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;/h3&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="986"></td><td class="line-content"><span class="html-tag">&lt;p&gt;</span>Generally speaking, the process of decompression is simply a matter of translating the stream of prefix codes to individual byte values, usually by traversing the Huffman tree node by node as each bit is read from the input stream (reaching a leaf node necessarily terminates the search for that particular byte value). Before this can take place, however, the Huffman tree must be somehow reconstructed. In the simplest case, where character frequencies are fairly predictable, the tree can be preconstructed (and even statistically adjusted on each compression cycle) and thus reused every time, at the expense of at least some measure of compression efficiency. Otherwise, the information to reconstruct the tree must be sent a priori. A naive approach might be to prepend the frequency count of each character to the compression stream. Unfortunately, the overhead in such a case could amount to several kilobytes, so this method has little practical use. If the data is compressed using <span class="html-tag">&lt;a <span class="html-attribute-name">href</span>="<a class="html-attribute-value html-external-link" target="_blank" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Canonical_Huffman_code" rel="noreferrer noopener">/wiki/Canonical_Huffman_code</a>" <span class="html-attribute-name">title</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">Canonical Huffman code</span>"&gt;</span>canonical encoding<span class="html-tag">&lt;/a&gt;</span>, the compression model can be precisely reconstructed with just <span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-element</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;span <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y</span>" <span class="html-attribute-name">style</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">display: none;</span>"&gt;</span><span class="html-tag">&lt;math <span class="html-attribute-name">xmlns</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML</span>"  <span class="html-attribute-name">alttext</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">{\displaystyle B2^{B}}</span>"&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="987"></td><td class="line-content">  <span class="html-tag">&lt;semantics&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="988"></td><td class="line-content">    <span class="html-tag">&lt;mrow <span class="html-attribute-name">class</span>="<span class="html-attribute-value">MJX-TeXAtom-ORD</span>"&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="989"></td><td class="line-content">      <span class="html-tag">&lt;mstyle <span <span class="html-tag">&lt;/mrow&gt;</span></td></tr><tr><td class="line-number" value="999"></td><td class="line-content">    <span class="html-tag">&lt;annotation <span
